# Analysis of US By County #

Updated: at 2020-09-05

For the US counties analysis, the list of all 3,143 counties (or equivalent) is sorted by the absolute number of deaths from highest to lowest.  This sorted list is then divided into two parts: counties with populations of 50,000 or more and smaller counties.

## Larger Population Counties ##

There were 990 larger population counties with a combined population of 288,662,059 (87.94% of the US population).  In these counties there have been 147,848 deaths (512.185 deaths/million) and 5,241,454 confirmed cases (18157.752 confirmed cases/million).  This group accounts for 89.93% of all US deaths and for 89.13% of all US cases.

24.12% of this group's deaths (21.69% of the total US deaths) occured in 13 counties in 10 states with a combined population of 37,287,218 (11.36% of the total US population):



The next 25.51% of this group's deaths (22.94% of the total US deaths) occured in 36 counties in 15 states with a combined population of 42,077,076 (12.82% of the total US population):



The next 25.34% of this group's deaths (22.78% of the total US deaths) occured in 103 counties in 31 states with a combined population of 70,482,642 (21.47% of the total US population)

The remaining 25.04% of this group's deaths (22.52% of the total US deaths) occured in 838 counties in 50 states with a combined population of 138,815,123 (42.29% of the total US population) 

## Smaller Population Counties ##

There were 2152 smaller population counties with a combined population of 39,577,464 (12.06% of the US population).  In these counties there have been 13,812 deaths (348.986 deaths/million) and 615,093 confirmed cases (15541.496 confirmed cases/million).  This group accounts for 8.40% of all US deaths and for 10.46% of all US cases.

25.00% of this group's deaths (2.10% of the total US deaths) occured in 69 counties in 17 states with a combined population of 2,392,232 (0.73% of the total US population):



The next 24.96% of this group's deaths (2.10% of the total US deaths) occured in 136 counties in 28 states with a combined population of 3,937,470 (1.20% of the total US population):



The next 25.04% of this group's deaths (2.10% of the total US deaths) occured in 266 counties in 34 states with a combined population of 6,328,609 (1.93% of the total US population)

The remaining 25.00% of this group's deaths (2.10% of the total US deaths) occured in 1,681 counties in 47 states with a combined population of 26,919,153 (8.20% of the total US population) 

## All US Counties ##

States and counties sorted by highest total number of deaths.  Counties with ten or fewer total deaths are not plotted nor are daily per capita rates compute for these counties.

The charts below are somewhat unusual.  The daily case and death rates per capita vary widely between US counties:  zero values occur frequently as do very large values.  We use log-log scales for these charts and add one (1) to the case and death rates before plotting.  Thus if a point is plotted at 1.0 the true value is zero, this difference is less and less visibile as rate values increase.  Adding 1.0 permits the use of log axis scales that best present these varying values.
